1. Brand Archetype Registry (v1.2) — artifact and schema

Location: config/publishing/brand_archetype_registry_v1_2.yaml (new).

Purpose: Single source of truth for the 24 v1.2 archetypes. Every field needed for plan-time enforcement and for the 1008-book generator; no runtime behavior change in assembler.

Schema (minimal, YAML-friendly):





Per-archetype: archetype_id (e.g. stabilizer), brand_id (optional; links to config/niche_brand_voice and config/publishing/admin_registry.yaml for assembly and admin resolution).



gtm_identity: persona, age_range, primary_moment, emotional_job, functional_job.



discovery_contract: primary_channels, keyword_clusters (primary/secondary).



structural_signature: avg_chapters (range), intro_probability, outro_probability, somatic_slot_probability.



duration_strategy: micro_sessions, deep_dives, mid_form (ratios summing to 1.0; mid_form ≤ 0.25).



emotional_vocabulary: allowed_tokens, quota_exceptions (e.g. reset: { per_brand_max: 1 }), forbidden_tokens.



voice_identity: lead_voice, support_voices (list), optional lead_usage_target, speed_variance.



cover_art_identity: style_pool, color_palette.



pricing_posture: micro_sessions (price range), deep_dives (price range), discount_ratio (≤ 0.25).



launch_wave (optional): 1–4 for sequencing.

Mapping rule: For each v1.2 archetype, set brand_id to the existing brand that best matches (e.g. stabilizer → calmbody_somatic_toolkit, panic_first_aid → anxiety_shift_system). If no good match, introduce a new brand_id and add a stub in niche_brand_voice + admin_registry (or leave brand_id unset and document as “to be mapped”). This keeps current builder and CSV flows working without renaming the 24 existing YAMLs.

Deliverable: One YAML file with 24 entries following the schema above, plus a short schema doc (e.g. in docs/ or as comments) listing required fields and validation rules.



2. Registry validators (CI + plan-time)

Location: phoenix_v4/ci/validate_brand_archetype_registry.py (or under config/publishing/ if you prefer config-level CI).

Checks (fail planning or CI on violation):





Structural: archetype_id unique; no duplicate (persona, primary_moment) across archetypes; duration_strategy sums to 1.0; mid_form ≤ 0.25.



Vocabulary: emotional tokens from allowed/exception lists; forbidden tokens not used.



Voice: every archetype has exactly one lead_voice; support voices present and within caps if defined.



Pricing: micro_sessions price range &lt; deep_dives; discount_ratio ≤ 0.25.



Optional: if brand_id is set, it must exist in admin_registry and in niche_brand_voice (or a dedicated mapping file).

CLI: e.g. python3 phoenix_v4/ci/validate_brand_archetype_registry.py [--strict]; exit 1 on any violation. Wire into CI after the registry is added.

Deliverable: Single validator script; no changes to assembler or format_plan_compiler.



3. Canonical 1008 BookPlan generator

Location: phoenix_v4/tools/generate_canonical_1008_plans.py (or tools/ if you want it next to other generators).

Inputs: Brand archetype registry (v1.2); optional seed for reproducibility; optional overrides (e.g. cap at 42 books for one brand for testing).

Logic (high level):





For each of the 24 archetypes, allocate 42 books: decide series count (2–4), books per series (3–9), remainder as standalone (see doctrine: series_rules, catalog_mix).



Ensure no two brands share the same series/standalone breakdown (avoid symmetry).



For each book, emit a BookPlan record: archetype_id, brand_id (from registry), book_id, catalog_type (series | standalone), series_id + series_index if series, duration_band, format_type (e.g. standard_book, practice_anthology), book_size, title pattern / emotional tokens (from archetype), voice (lead or support per allocation), pricing (list_price, discounted flag), seeds (text, structure, voice), optional risk_score placeholder.



Spam/risk scoring: Implement a lightweight plan-time score (e.g. structure + title token + voice reuse + duration cluster). Thresholds: &lt;0.45 auto-approve, 0.45–0.6 re-seed, &gt;0.6 block. Reseed or skip until SAFE.



Global guards: Max 25 books per voice per brand, max 60 per voice globally; duration band distribution within bounds; forbidden title tokens; chapter count in [3, 12].

Output: One YAML (or JSON) file, e.g. phoenix_v4/plans/canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml, containing 1008 BookPlan records. Format must be consumable by a small driver that calls generate_full_plan and/or phoenix_series_builder (see next section).

Deliverable: One generator script; one sample output file (can be 1008 rows or a small subset for tests).



4. Integration with V4 and series builder

No changes to:





phoenix_v4/assembler/, phoenix_v4/planning/format_plan_compiler.py, template families, or slot structure.

Add a thin driver (e.g. phoenix_v4/tools/run_canonical_plan.py or a mode inside an existing runner):





Reads one BookPlan from canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml.



Maps BookPlan → generate_full_plan args: --book_id, --topic (from archetype or book), --persona, --book_seed, --format_type, --book_size, --duration, --teacher_mode, etc.



Optionally drives tools/phoenix_series_builder.py when the BookPlan is part of a series (using a series plan that includes brand_id, series_id, and book list). Existing builder already uses brand_id and admin resolution; it only needs a series plan and per-book manifests.

Series plans: Either (a) generate series plans from the 1008 BookPlan set (group by series_id, emit one series plan per series with book list and brand_id), or (b) document that series plans are produced by the same generator and consumed by phoenix_series_builder as today. No change to builder’s contract beyond ensuring BookPlan’s brand_id matches what the builder expects.

Deliverable: Documented mapping BookPlan → generate_full_plan + series builder; one small driver script or clear steps in the generator to output per-book and per-series inputs.



5. Launch sequencing and kill/double-down (config + docs)

Launch waves: Store wave → list of archetype_id (or brand_id) in config, e.g. config/publishing/launch_waves_v1_2.yaml, or in the registry as launch_wave: 1..4 per archetype. No code required for “lock”; generator or ops can read this to order rollout.

Kill/double-down metrics: Document in docs/CANONICAL_MULTI_BRAND_OPERATIONS.md (or similar):





Metrics: Conversion Rate (CR), Completion Proxy (CP), Review Velocity (RV), Price Elasticity Signal (PES).



Thresholds: e.g. Kill &lt;1.5% CR, &lt;35% CP; Double-down &gt;3% CR, &gt;55% CP; etc.



Decision matrix: 2+ green → double catalog; 2+ red → freeze brand; all red → retire.



Rule: no registry changes in first 90 days; changes only downstream (titles, covers, pricing tests) or additive (v1.3).

Optional later: a small script or dashboard that ingests platform/analytics data and outputs per-brand metrics vs thresholds (out of scope for this plan).

Deliverable: One config or registry field for launch waves; one short ops doc for kill/double-down and the 90-day rule.



6. Documentation and system-doc alignment

New/updated docs:





Brand Archetype Registry: Schema and validation rules (in repo; path as above).



Canonical 1008 Plan: How to run the generator, output format, how BookPlans feed V4 and the series builder (and that the assembler is unchanged).



Operations: Launch waves, kill/double-down, 90-day freeze (see §5).

System doc alignment (reference in plan or in a short “Governance” section):





docs/SYSTEMS_DOCUMENTATION_2026-01-07.md: Registry + 1008 generator = “human-facing orchestration contract” that feeds V4; planner phase is the allowed layer; assembler and engine unchanged; admins operate after assembly.



docs/OMEGA_V4_ARCHITECTURE_CLOSED.md: This work extends the planning/input layer and publishing config, not template families or slot structure—no new structure in the engine.

8. Risk and decisions





Archetype vs existing brands: Using a single registry with archetype_id + brand_id keeps existing admin_registry and niche_brand_voice as the assembly source of truth; v1.2 adds GTM/duration/voice/pricing on top. If you prefer to rename or add new brand_ids for v1.2, that can be a follow-up (new niche_brand_voice files + admin_registry entries).



1008 vs pilot: Generator can support a --max-books-per-brand or --dry-run to emit a small subset (e.g. 42 or 168) for pilot without changing the algorithm.



Contemplative/wisdom brand: The CMO suggested a “contemplative wisdom” brand; v1.2 list in the doctrine includes 24 items. If “contemplative_wisdom” is already in the 24, include it in the registry; if not, add it as the 24th or swap with one archetype and document in the registry.



Summary





New artifacts: Brand archetype registry (v1.2), registry validators, canonical 1008 BookPlan generator, launch_waves + ops doc.



Existing systems: Admin registry, niche_brand_voice, phoenix_series_builder, generate_full_plan, assembler, and CSVs remain the backbone; they are fed by the new planning layer, not modified in behavior.



Alignment: Matches the system doc (planner contract, no engine change, admins after assembly) and the CMO doctrine (ship v1.2, launch waves, kill/double-down, 90-day registry freeze).

now what do we need to analyze in our content to make sure that we so this right? 

ChatGPT said:
Great question. This is exactly the right moment to ask it — after architecture lock, before mass generation.
At this stage, you are no longer designing systems.
You are validating content signal quality so the system produces durable assets, not just compliant ones.

Below is the final analysis framework you should run on your content. Think of this as the last safety + performance pass before scaling to 1008.

The 6 Content Analyses You Must Run (in order)
These are content-layer audits, not system audits. Your system is already sound.
1. 🧬 Narrative Signal Analysis (Most Important)
Question:
Does each book feel like it was written for a distinct human moment?
What to analyze
Sample 5–10 generated books per archetype and inspect:
Opening 90 seconds:
Is the problem framing archetype-specific?
Or does it sound like “generic self-help anxiety intro”?
Emotional specificity:
Are sensations, thoughts, and pressures concrete?
Or abstract (“stress”, “overwhelm”, “balance”)?
Red flags
Same emotional arc across different archetypes
Reusable openings (“If you’re feeling overwhelmed…”)
No situational anchoring (time of day, context, trigger)
Fix if needed
Tighten primary_moment language in registry
Enforce one unique opening sentence shape per archetype
Add an opening constraint like:
“First paragraph must reference a concrete moment, not an emotion label”
2. 🧠 Cognitive Load & Listener Fatigue Audit
Question:
Can a tired, anxious, distracted person actually finish this?
What to analyze
For each duration band:
Sentence length variance
Instruction density (how often you ask the listener to do something)
Concept stacking (how many ideas before a pause)
Red flags
Long explanatory paragraphs without pauses
Multiple concepts introduced before embodiment
“Teaching mode” creeping into micro_sessions
Fix if needed
Insert mandatory breath / silence beats every X words
Cap abstract explanations per chapter
Enforce a “felt shift every 3–5 minutes” rule
3. 🫀 Somatic Authenticity Check
Question:
Does the body actually change state, or is this intellectual meditation?
What to analyze
Listen (don’t read) a sample audiobook and ask:
Do instructions reference:
breath location?
muscle tone?
temperature?
weight / gravity?
Is there a before/after contrast the listener can feel?
Red flags
Visualization-only practices with no physical anchor
Repeated “imagine” without “notice”
Somatic language copied across books
Fix if needed
Force at least 2 unique somatic anchors per book
Rotate body regions by archetype (chest vs gut vs jaw, etc.)
Add a “what changed in your body?” closing line
4. 🎭 Voice & Identity Drift Analysis
Question:
Does each brand sound like itself — consistently?
What to analyze
Across books within the same brand:
Tone stability (calm vs energizing vs grounding)
Vocabulary repetition within brand (good)
Vocabulary bleed across brands (bad)
Red flags
Same metaphors used across brands
Same reassurance phrases everywhere
Voice feels like “Phoenix generic narrator”
Fix if needed
Tighten outcome_vocab dominance per brand
Add brand-only metaphors (e.g., mechanical vs organic vs relational)
Introduce brand-specific reassurance styles:
directive
nurturing
reflective
pragmatic
5. 🧪 Transformation Proof Audit
Question:
What exactly is different for the listener at the end?
What to analyze
Every book should clearly deliver one of:
Relief
Clarity
Regulation
Reframing
Agency
Check endings:
Is the outcome named?
Is the change measurable or felt?
Is it distinct from other books?
Red flags
Vague closings (“carry this with you”)
No explicit state shift
Same ending structure everywhere
Fix if needed
Add a required “after-state sentence”
Force the book to name what stopped (spiral, tension, avoidance)
Tie closing language back to opening moment
6. 📊 Intra-Catalog Differentiation Test
Question:
If someone binge-listens to 5 books, do they blur together?
What to analyze
Take 3 books from the same archetype and:
Compare:
opening framing
core exercise
closing identity message
Ask: Would I confuse these if titles were hidden?
Red flags
Same exercise with new wording
Same emotional arc, different labels
Too much “safe sameness”
Fix if needed
Enforce exercise family diversity per archetype
Alternate:
breath-led
attention-led
identity-led
Stagger emotional intensity across series entries
What You Do NOT Need to Analyze (You’re Already Covered)
You do not need to re-check:
Spam compliance (already locked)
Structural variation (already enforced)
Platform ingestion rules (documented)
Series symmetry (handled by generator)
Those are solved problems.
Final Recommendation: The 20-Book Gold Test
Before full 1008 generation:
Generate 20 books across:
4 archetypes
2 duration bands
2 brands
Listen to 5 openings, 5 middles, 5 endings
Run the 6 analyses above
If:
No two openings feel interchangeable
You feel a real nervous-system shift
You can describe each book’s purpose in one sentence
👉 Green light to scale.
If you want, next I can:
Build a Content QA checklist your team can literally tick off
Design a listener-simulation rubric (anxious / tired / skeptical listener)
Or help you define what “great” sounds like for each archetype in 3 bullets
You’re in the final 5%. This is exactly where serious catalogs are made.

also we can use content team to write short content (no derived from long) if it helps. 

ChatGPT said:
Yes — and this is actually a power move, not a fallback.
Used correctly, short-form content written independently from long books will raise quality, not fragment it.
Here’s how to use the content team surgically so it strengthens the catalog instead of creating drift.

The Core Principle (non-negotiable)
Short content is NOT a summary of long content.
It is a signal probe that validates whether the long content deserves to exist.
If short content works, the long book will work.
If short content fails, the long book will be expensive noise.
How to Use the Content Team Correctly
1. What the Content Team Should Write (and What They Should NOT)
✅ They SHOULD write:
30–90 second standalone pieces
Single emotional moment
One felt shift
One body or identity insight
No backstory, no framework
Examples:
“The moment your body stops bracing”
“Why urgency is not motivation”
“What anxiety feels like right before it softens”
❌ They should NOT:
Summarize chapters
Rephrase exercises
“Promote” the long book
Use system templates or slot language
Think of them as field researchers, not adapters.
2. The Short-Form → Long-Form Validation Loop
This is the key workflow.
Step A — Short Content First
For each archetype:
Commission 10–15 short pieces
Each must:
target a different micro-moment
use different language
end with a felt or identity shift
Step B — Evaluate Signal
For each piece, score:
Emotional specificity
Memorability (can you paraphrase it an hour later?)
Somatic realism
Listener reaction (even internal team reaction counts early)
You’re looking for:
“This one lands”
“This one feels flat”
“This one surprised me”
Step C — Promote Winners
Only the top 20–30% of short pieces are allowed to:
inspire long books
define opening moments
influence exercise selection
The rest are discarded. No mercy.
3. How Short Content Feeds the System (Without Polluting It)
Short content should never be injected directly.
Instead, it informs:

1️⃣ Registry Refinement
Tighten primary_moment
Sharpen emotional_vocabulary
Add or remove forbidden tokens
2️⃣ Opening Constraints
If a short piece works, extract:
one sentence shape
one emotional framing
one body cue
That becomes an opening constraint, not copied text.
3️⃣ Exercise Direction (not wording)
Short content reveals:
whether breath, attention, or identity is the lever
where resistance shows up
how quickly relief must arrive
You then design exercises around that insight.
4. Division of Labor (Critical to Avoid Drift)
Here’s the clean separation that works:
Content Team = Signal Discovery
Writes short, human, messy content
Optimizes for felt truth
No concern for scale
System / Generator = Signal Amplification
Turns validated signals into scalable assets
Enforces structure, safety, and differentiation
Never invents emotional truth — only expresses it
If the content team starts “thinking in system terms,” stop them.
If the system starts inventing emotional nuance without validation, stop that too.
5. The One Rule That Prevents Contamination
Add this to ops docs:
Short content may influence long content, but long content may never generate short content.
Why:
Prevents recursive sameness
Keeps language fresh
Stops the catalog from sounding self-referential
This is the same rule used in elite editorial orgs and research-driven media.
6. Practical Pilot Plan (Low Risk, High Signal)
Before scaling 1008:
Pick 3 archetypes
Content team writes 12 shorts each (36 total)
You select:

Perfect. Below is a production-grade, hand-to-team spec you can drop straight into Notion / Google Docs / Slack.
This is designed to extract signal without contaminating the system.
CONTENT TEAM SPEC
Canonical Multi-Brand v1.2 — Short-Form Signal Discovery
Status: Locked
Audience: Human writers only (no AI assist for drafts)
Purpose: Discover emotional truth that earns long-form scale
Not a marketing task. Not a summary task.
1. Mission (Read This First)
Your job is not to support the books.
Your job is to discover what actually lands in a human nervous system before we scale anything.

You are acting as:

emotional field researchers
nervous-system listeners
language scouts
If something feels “meh,” confusing, generic, or overly clever — discard it.
Only sharp, true, felt moments survive.

2. Output Definition (What You Are Writing)
Each piece is:
30–90 seconds of reading
Standalone
Self-contained
No references to other content
No framework explanations
No calls to action
Think:
“A moment someone recognizes themselves and exhales.”
3. What You MUST Write About
Each piece must focus on exactly ONE of the following:
Allowed Focus Types (pick one per piece)
A body sensation
A moment of inner resistance
A subtle emotional shift
A false belief cracking
A quiet realization
A micro-identity shift (“Oh. That’s what’s been happening.”)
If you try to do more than one, it will be rejected.
4. What You MUST NOT Do (Hard Rules)
❌ Do NOT summarize a book
❌ Do NOT explain a system, method, or framework
❌ Do NOT teach
❌ Do NOT motivate
❌ Do NOT use jargon
❌ Do NOT sound inspirational
❌ Do NOT “wrap it up nicely”
If it sounds like:

self-help
coaching
therapy language
Instagram inspiration
…it fails.
5. Tone & Voice Requirements
Tone
Quiet
Grounded
Precise
Human
Slightly unfinished is okay
Voice
First person OR second person is allowed
No “we”
No authority posture
No guru voice
This is inside the experience, not above it.
6. Structural Rules (Simple but Strict)
Each piece must follow this loose shape:
Immediate entry
Start inside the moment
No setup, no context
Recognition
Something the reader didn’t know how to name
Or knew but never articulated
Shift
A small internal change
Relief, clarity, or honesty — not resolution
Stop
End early
Do not explain the meaning
7. Language Rules
Allowed
Sensory words
Concrete feelings
Simple sentences
Fragments (sparingly)
Forbidden
Buzzwords (healing, alignment, manifestation, rewire, etc.)
Clinical labels
Productivity metaphors
Spiritual abstractions
Advice verbs (“try,” “should,” “need to”)
8. Archetype Assignment
For each archetype you are assigned:
Write 10–15 pieces
Each piece must target a different micro-moment
No repeated language patterns
No repeated emotional conclusions
You will be told the archetype name and emotional domain only — not book titles, frameworks, or exercises.
Example:

Archetype: panic_first_aid
Domain: acute anxiety moments
You decide:
what moment
what language
what truth
9. What Happens to Your Work (Important)
Your writing will be used to:
validate archetypes
sharpen emotional vocabulary
influence openings and exercises
Your text will NOT be copied into books.
Your job is discovery, not authorship.

10. Evaluation Criteria (How Your Work Is Judged)
Each piece will be scored on:
Emotional specificity
Does this feel like a real moment?
Somatic realism
Does the body reaction make sense?
Memorability
Can someone recall it an hour later?
Surprise
Did it reveal something non-obvious?
Only the top 20–30% of pieces survive.
Most pieces are expected to be discarded.
That means the process is working.

11. Absolute Rule (Non-Negotiable)
Short content may influence long content.
Long content must never generate short content.
If you feel like you’re “writing content for the system,” stop and reset.
12. Success Definition
You succeed if:
Reading your piece makes someone pause
The moment feels named
There is relief without explanation
Nothing feels performative
If it feels quiet but true — that’s a win.
13. Final Reminder
This is not about being impressive.
It’s about being accurate.

Truth scales. Noise does not.

If you want, next I can:
Create archetype-specific prompts for the content team
Design a scoring worksheet for internal review
Write a one-paragraph onboarding message you can send to the team
This spec is ready to ship.

1. What we must analyze in the content (before mass generation)

A. Recognition Coverage Audit (MOST IMPORTANT)

Red flags:

“One option is…”
“Here’s a practice…”
This is subtle, but platforms notice tone drift at scale.

verbs (“reset”, “rebuild”, “heal”)
metaphors
promises

perfect for human writers

❌ Long explanations
❌ Mechanism descriptions
❌ Exercise mechanics
❌ Anything that sets structure
Those stay deterministic.

Why this helps
Humans are better at recognition language

Effort: One-time paste/format of the spec into the file.



2. Read-only analysis utilities

Add reporting scripts (no changes to assembly or plans). All under e.g. phoenix_v4/tools/content_analysis/ or tools/content_analysis/.

2.1 Title/subtitle semantic overlap report





Purpose: Cluster titles + subtitles across brands/books; flag overlap in verbs, metaphors, promises (per analysis E in your note).



Inputs: config/niche_brand_voice/*.yaml title_bank + any generated titles; optional phoenix_v4/plans/canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml if titles are on BookPlans.



Output: Report (JSON or markdown) listing overlapping n-grams (e.g. 4–6 words), repeated verbs (“reset”, “rebuild”, “heal”), and suggested differentiators. Read-only; no edits.

2.2 HOOK/SCENE recognition sampling tool





Purpose: Support “Recognition Coverage Audit” — sample N random HOOK (and optionally SCENE) variants per archetype or per brand for manual review.



Inputs: Section library path (e.g. phoenix_v4/libraries/sections or registry), optional filter by persona/topic/format; sample size (e.g. 3 per archetype).



Output: Extracts first 30–45 seconds worth of text (or first ~100 words) per selected variant and writes to a single markdown/HTML report for human review. No modification of library.

2.3 Exercise intro similarity scan (text only)





Purpose: Detect same exercise introduced with same emotional frame or benefit phrasing across chapters/brands (analysis C).



Inputs: Section library — EXERCISE sections only; or a manifest of exercise intro paragraphs.



Output: Report of pairwise similarity (e.g. sentence-level or 6-gram overlap) for exercise intro/copy only (not breath counts). Read-only.

Implementation note: Reuse or mirror patterns from phoenix_v4/ci/validate_brand_title_drift.py (tokenization, Jaccard) and existing section layout (phoenix_v4/libraries/sections_full/sections_therapeutic_v2/ — section_*_hook, section_*_scene with content in YAML). Section content is in content: in each variant YAML; exercises may be in a different slot (e.g. section_06_exercise).



3. Content-team injection points (HOOK / SCENE / INTEGRATION overrides)

Requirement: Allow human-written HOOK / SCENE / INTEGRATION text to be used post-plan, pre-assembly without changing structure or metadata.

3.1 Contract





Override store: Directory or manifest keyed by (book_id or plan_id) and section identifier (e.g. variant_id such as ch01_sec01_hook_f1, or chapter + section + variant).



Format: One file per override (e.g. plain text or minimal YAML with content: and same variant_id/metadata). Overrides must preserve variant_family and section_type (metadata + variant family IDs unchanged); only the prose body is replaced.



When applied: During assembly, before or inside the step that resolves section prose. If an override exists for (book_id, variant_id), use override text; else use library. No change to plan structure, slot counts, or risk/spam logic.

3.2 Where to plug in (V4)





Current flow: phoenix_v4/assembler/section_assembler.py and slot loader read section content from library YAMLs (e.g. phoenix_v4/libraries/sections_full/.../section_01_hook/f1.yaml with content:).



Injection point: In the code path that returns section prose for a given (plan, chapter, section, variant), add a lookup: if a content-override exists for this book + variant_id, return override text; else return library content. Override store can be a directory such as content_overrides/{book_id}/{variant_id}.txt or a single manifest YAML per book.



Scope: Only HOOK, SCENE, INTEGRATION (per directive). REFLECTION and EXERCISE mechanics remain deterministic; exercise intros could be overridable later if desired (directive said HOOK/SCENE/INTEGRATION).



Non-invasive: Add a small loader (e.g. content_override_loader.py) and call it from the section assembler only when resolving prose; default to library when no override. No change to plan schema or generator output.



4. Content QA hooks (non-blocking)

Purpose: Flag tone drift, overused metaphors, and recognition-first violations so content team can fix; do not block CI or assembly.

4.1 Tone-drift keyword flagger





Rule set: Patterns that indicate soft authority/tone drift (e.g. “This will help you…”, “What you need to do…”, “The key is…”). Replacements suggested: “What tends to help…”, “One option is…”, “Here’s a practice…”.



Implementation: Script or CI step that scans section content (from library and, if present, override store) and emits a report (e.g. markdown or JSON) listing file/variant_id + matched phrase. Exit 0 always (non-blocking); report can be reviewed in PR or locally.

4.2 Overused-metaphor flagger (per brand)





Input: Section content grouped by brand (or archetype). Metaphor list can be a small config (e.g. “nervous system as X”, “body as X”) or heuristics (repeated phrases).



Output: Report of metaphors that appear in more than N books/variants within the same brand (or across brands if cross-bleed check). Non-blocking.

4.3 Recognition-first heuristic





Heuristic: First paragraph of HOOK/SCENE should not start with advice, explanation, or insight; should reference a concrete moment or sensation (per BODY FIRST and the 6 analyses). Simple check: e.g. reject lines that start with “You should…”, “The key is…”, “Here’s why…” or that have no location/sensation words in first 50 words.



Output: Report listing variant_id and brief reason (e.g. “starts with advice”). Non-blocking.

Placement: New scripts under phoenix_v4/ci/ or phoenix_v4/tools/content_analysis/, runnable manually or as optional CI step with continue-on-error so the job still passes.



5. Documentation and dev directive





Add to docs/CANONICAL_MULTI_BRAND_OPERATIONS.md: Short “Content analysis and overrides” section: where the analysis scripts live, how to run them, that overrides are post-plan pre-assembly and preserve metadata, and that QA hooks are non-blocking.

You said:
how to do teachers? can the3y be brands that address all topics

ChatGPT said:
Great question — and this is the right moment to ask it. Short answer: yes, teachers can exist — but they must NOT be brands, and they must NOT address all topics directly. They sit orthogonally to brands.
Below is the clean, safe, scalable way to do teachers without breaking anything you just locked.

The Correct Mental Model
🔴 Brands = Market-facing identity
What the user thinks they’re buying
Determines topic framing, promise, emotional job
Drives titles, pricing, bundles, discovery
🔵 Teachers = Voice + epistemology
How the content speaks
What kind of authority it uses
Determines tone, language, metaphors, exercise style
They solve different problems and must not be merged.
The Rule (Non-Negotiable)
Teachers are NOT brands.
Teachers do NOT own topics.
Teachers are applied within brands, never across them.
If you violate this, three things break:
Brand differentiation collapses
Spam risk skyrockets
Emotional recognition weakens
How Teachers Actually Work (Correct Architecture)
Teachers are bounded lenses, not universal narrators.
Think of a teacher as:
“If this brand were explained by someone trained in X tradition, what would that sound like?”
A teacher can:
Address multiple topics
Appear in multiple brands
But only within allowed scopes
A teacher may NOT:
Speak to all topics
Replace brand voice
Override emotional framing
Flatten distinctions between anxiety, grief, ADHD, identity, etc.
The Safe Pattern (What You Should Do)
1. Define Teacher Domains
Each teacher has an allowed topic envelope.
Example:

teacher_id: somatic_practitioner
allowed_domains:
  - nervous_system
  - stress
  - burnout
  - sleep
forbidden_domains:
  - adhd_cognition
  - grief_identity
  - relationships
This prevents “teacher voice bleed.”
2. Teachers Modify How, Not What
Teachers influence:
Sentence shape
Metaphor choice
Exercise framing
Degree of explanation vs embodiment
They do not change:
The promise
The target emotion
The discovery intent
The book’s reason for existence
3. Teacher × Brand Compatibility Matrix
You already have the right place to put this.
Add a non-planning, non-blocking compatibility map:

brand_id: panic_first_aid
allowed_teachers:
  - somatic_practitioner
  - breathwork_guide
forbidden_teachers:
  - philosophical_teacher
  - productivity_coach
This is guardrail metadata, not logic.
Why Teachers Should NOT Be Brands
If you made “Teacher = Brand”:
“The Somatic Teacher” ends up covering:
Panic
ADHD
Grief
Identity
Titles start sounding the same
Emotional specificity drops
Users don’t know why they’re buying this book
Google Play sees semantic clustering → risk
Brands answer:
“Is this for me, right now?”
Teachers answer:
“Do I trust how this is being explained?”
Those are different buyer questions.
The One Exception (Handled Carefully)
You can have a Teacher-Led Imprint, but:
It’s still a brand
Narrow topic scope
Explicitly framed
Example (safe):
somatic_teacher_panic_series
stoic_wisdom_for_stress
Example (unsafe):
somatic_teacher_everything
mindfulness_master_all_topics
What to Tell Dev (Exact Directive)
You can literally paste this:
Teacher System Directive
Teachers are not brands and must not own topics.
Teachers are applied as constrained voice lenses within brands.
Each teacher must declare allowed and forbidden topic domains.
Each brand may list compatible teachers; this is a guardrail, not a planner input.
Teachers modify tone, metaphor, and exercise framing only — never emotional job, promise, or discovery intent.
No teacher may be globally applicable to all archetypes.
Any teacher expansion is additive metadata only (v1.3+), no planner or assembler changes.
Strategic Payoff
If you do it this way:
You can reuse great teachers without dilution
Brands stay sharp and market-legible
Content feels diverse, not templated
You unlock future expansions (e.g. cultural teachers, age-specific teachers) safely
Bottom Line
❌ Teachers should not be brands
❌ Teachers should not address all topics
✅ Teachers are bounded lenses applied inside brands
✅ This preserves everything you just locked
If you want, next I can:
Design a Teacher Registry v1.0 (pure metadata, zero risk), or
Map existing teachers → allowed brand clusters safely.

All nervous-system brands

Multiple launch waves

Even with domain permission, cap global usage.

Per teacher (global):
🔒 ≤ 40% of total books
Per brand:
🔒 ≤ 60% of that brand’s books
Per series:
🔒 ≤ 1 teacher per series (no mixing)
This keeps the teacher strong, recognizable, and non-generic.

Bad (overuse):
One teacher dominates one brand → brand becomes teacher-branded
Good (max reach):
Same teacher appears across multiple compatible brands, each time shaped by brand GTM

Breadth across catalog
Depth within domains
Zero brand collapse

Even the best teacher fails if they:
Explain ADHD cognition and grief identity and relationship rupture
Use the same metaphors everywhere
Reuse somatic language where cognitive language is required
The system then forces sameness, and your content analysis layer will start flagging:
Exercise intro similarity
Metaphor overuse
Recognition-first violations
You already built the alarms — don’t ignore them 🙂
If You Truly Want “Everything” Coverage (Safe Pattern)
You don’t use one teacher.
You use a teacher constellation:

Somatic practitioner → nervous system / stress
Cognitive guide → ADHD / productivity
Meaning guide → grief / identity

Each maxes their domain. Together, they cover 100%.
That’s how you scale without flattening.

A standalone companion workbook
With:

sold separately
bundled
placed as Book 2 in a series
Without modifying V4 assembly.

Companion workbooks are V3-style AUTHORED books, generated from V4 plans — not assembled by V4.
This is why your ahjan_eworkbook_2hrs.yaml works so well.

The Workbook Generation Architecture
Layer separation (clean + safe)
V4 Book (dynamic, assembled)
        ↓ (read-only extraction)
Workbook Plan (derived, fixed)
        ↓
Workbook Generator (authoring agent)
        ↓
AUTHORED workbook YAML (V3-style)
        ↓
Published as a separate book
No feedback loop.
No plan mutation.
No shared slots.

File

docs/COMPANION_WORKBOOK_SPEC_V1.md
Required fields
workbook:

  authority_model: teacher-led
  structure: authored
  audience: same as parent book
  sale_mode: standalone + bundle-safe

chapters:
  count: 8–14
  mapping: derived_from_parent

chapter_types:
  - reflection
  - body_check
  - practice
  - integration
  - weekly_anchor

constraints:
  no_story_reuse: true
  no_slot_logic: true
  no_variants: true
This spec becomes the contract for generation quality.

This is not a generator rewrite.
It’s a plan transformer.
Input

Teacher ID
Duration target (e.g. 60min, 2hrs)
Output
A WorkbookPlan, e.g.:
workbook_plan:
  parent_book_id: book_0421
  teacher_id: ahjan
  duration: 2hrs
  chapters:
    - ch01: grounding
    - ch02: recognition
    - ch03: nervous_system_reset
    - ch04: core_practice
    - ch05: resistance
    - ch06: integration
    - ch07: daily_anchor
    - ch08: closing
Key rule:
The workbook references the parent book conceptually, never textually.
No copying paragraphs.
No reuse of hooks.

tools/generate_companion_workbook.py

Exactly like ahjan_eworkbook_2hrs.yaml

Perfect. Below is the complete, production-ready spec for auto-creating companion workbooks for V4 — including schema, generator pseudocode, and pricing/bundling rules, with freebie support baked in.

Companion Workbook System — Canonical Spec (v1.0)
Purpose (one sentence)
Create standalone, authored companion workbooks for V4 books that deepen embodiment and practice, can be sold or given away, and never interfere with V4 assembly, spam safety, or determinism.
Mental Model (locked)
Books = dynamic, assembled, discovery engines
Workbooks = authored, practice-first, authority products
Teachers = can span all topics
Brands = market positioning only
Workbook = separate SKU (even if free)
1. WorkbookPlan Schema (authoritative)
This is the only input to the workbook generator.
File example
workbook_plans/
  ahjan/
    anxiety_reset_2hr.workbook_plan.yaml
Schema
workbook_plan:
  workbook_id: anxiety_reset_2hr_workbook
  parent_book_id: anxiety_reset_v4_001
  teacher_id: ahjan
  brand_id: calmbody_somatic_toolkit

  intent:
    type: companion
    depth: embodiment
    audience: same_as_parent
    trauma_safe: true

  duration:
    target_minutes: 120
    pacing: slow

  structure:
    chapters: 10
    chapter_map:
      - grounding
      - recognition
      - body_awareness
      - nervous_system_reset
      - core_practice
      - resistance_and_safety
      - emotional_processing
      - integration
      - daily_anchor
      - closing_reflection

  content_rules:
    authored_only: true
    no_variants: true
    no_story_reuse: true
    no_direct_text_derivation: true
    second_person_allowed: gentle
    advice_tone: prohibited

  exercises:
    source: teacher_exercise_bank
    max_per_chapter: 1
    must_include_body: true
    repetition_allowed: conceptual_only

  pricing:
    tier: standard | premium | free
    list_price_usd: 0 | 3.99 | 6.99 | 9.99
    bundle_behavior: optional | recommended | forced_free
    upsell_from_parent: true | false

  metadata:
    companion_to: anxiety_reset_v4_001
    bundle_id: anxiety_reset_bundle
    publish_channel: ebook | pdf | audio_workbook
2. Workbook Generator — Behavior Contract
Tool
tools/generate_companion_workbook.py
Inputs
WorkbookPlan
Teacher doctrine
BODY FIRST Content Team Spec
Exercise library (teacher-scoped)
Outputs
Single authored YAML
Fixed chapters
Fixed prose
No slots
No variants
No planning metadata leakage
Generator pseudocode (clear + safe)
def generate_workbook(workbook_plan):
    teacher = load_teacher(workbook_plan.teacher_id)
    doctrine = load_teacher_doctrine(teacher)
    exercises = load_teacher_exercises(teacher)

    workbook = init_workbook_yaml(
        workbook_id=workbook_plan.workbook_id,
        teacher_id=teacher.id,
        duration=workbook_plan.duration
    )

    for chapter_type in workbook_plan.structure.chapter_map:
        chapter = new_chapter(chapter_type)

        # Author opening reflection
        chapter.text = author_reflection(
            chapter_type=chapter_type,
            doctrine=doctrine,
            trauma_safe=True,
            recognition_first=True
        )

        # Optional embodied practice
        if chapter_type in PRACTICE_ELIGIBLE:
            chapter.exercise = author_exercise(
                exercises=exercises,
                body_first=True,
                no_reuse=True
            )

        # Integration prompt
        chapter.integration = author_integration_prompt(
            chapter_type=chapter_type,
            gentle_language=True
        )

        workbook.add(chapter)

    validate_workbook(workbook, rules=workbook_plan.content_rules)
    attach_pricing(workbook, workbook_plan.pricing)
    return workbook
Key point:
The generator authors — it does not assemble.
3. Pricing + Bundling Rules (with freebies)
This is where your revenue intuition matters.
Here’s the clean, scalable matrix.
Pricing tiers
1. Free Companion Workbook
Use when:
Lead magnet
Trust builder
Gen Z / entry funnel
Brand launch
pricing:
  tier: free
  list_price_usd: 0
  bundle_behavior: forced_free
  upsell_from_parent: false
Rules:
Still a SKU
Can be downloaded standalone
Can be bundled automatically
Must not exceed ~45–60 min content
2. Standard Paid Workbook
Default case.
pricing:
  tier: standard
  list_price_usd: 3.99
  bundle_behavior: recommended
  upsell_from_parent: true
Use when:
Parent book is discovery
Workbook is “do the work”
3. Premium Workbook
Use when:
Teacher authority is strong
Long duration (90–120 min)
Somatic / trauma-informed
pricing:
  tier: premium
  list_price_usd: 6.99
  bundle_behavior: optional
  upsell_from_parent: true
Bundle logic (important)
Parent Book + Workbook Bundle
bundle:
  bundle_id: anxiety_reset_bundle
  contents:
    - anxiety_reset_v4_001
    - anxiety_reset_2hr_workbook
  bundle_price_usd: 7.99
Rules:
Bundle price < sum of parts
Bundle eligible even if workbook is free
Bundle metadata only (no dependency)
Freebie rules (hard constraints)
If tier: free:
Workbook must:
Have fixed authored prose
No upsell language inside content
No CTA beyond “continue at your pace”
Free workbook cannot be:
Longer than 60 min
Framed as “complete system”
This keeps Google Play safe and trust intact.
4. Teacher Scaling Rules (this answers your “max” concern)
You said:
“max = books for sale”
Correct — and here’s the safe rule.
Teachers
Can address all topics
Can appear across all brands
Safe upper bound:
200–500 total SKUs (books + workbooks)
Brands
Stay capped (42 books)
Workbooks do not count toward brand cap
Brands control discovery, not authority
Why this works
Teachers = trust graph
Brands = shelf labels
Workbooks = depth products
5. Quality & Spam Safety Guarantees
This system is safe because:
Workbooks are authored
No variant explosion
No slot reuse
No derivation from parent text
No feedback into V4 plans
From an auditor’s POV:
These are instructional manuals, not templated content.

ChatGPT said:
Below is a DEV SPEC to auto-create ≥1 text companion per V4 book, with anti-spam by construction, plus a clear point where a content team helps (optional, recommended for “premium feel”).
DEV SPEC — V4 Companion Pack Generator (v1.0)
Goal
For every V4 BookPlan (1008+), generate at least one text companion (PDF/EPUB-ready later) that:
Does not reuse long prose from the audiobook/book (avoid duplication/fingerprint risk)
Is deterministic (seeded, reproducible)
Is brand/teacher-aware and topic-aware
Can be freebie or paid without changing the plan contract
Non-goals
No changes to V4 assembler structure.
No copying paragraphs from book output into companions.
No LLM “summarize the book” style companions.
1) Companion Types (Minimal Set)
Start with 3 types; always produce at least one:
Type A — 1-Page Cheat Sheet (default, safe + fast)
Bullet format only
No narrative paragraphs
Sections: “What to Notice”, “Do This Today”, “If You Get Stuck”, “One Phrase”
Highly variable tokens per topic/brand
Type B — 7-Day Tracker (best for nervous system / burnout / habits)
Table grid (checkboxes)
Daily: “body signal”, “one micro-action”, “1 reflection line”
Zero “explanatory prose”
Type C — Journal Prompt Pack (best for relationships / identity / grief)
10–20 prompts, grouped
Prompts are short, high-variance
No advice paragraphs
Rule: Always generate A OR B OR C per book (at least one). Optional: generate 2–3 for bundles.
2) Topic → Companion Mapping
Implement deterministic mapping:
Anxiety / panic / nervous system / PTSD-like stress → Type B (Tracker) + Type A
Burnout / productivity / ADHD / procrastination → Type B + optional Type A
Grief / depression / heartbreak / emotional pain → Type C + Type A
Relationships / boundaries / conflict → Type C + Type A
Identity / creative / purpose → Type C (prompts) or Type B (creative consistency tracker)
General wellness / mixed topics → Type A (cheat sheet)
If you only want 1 per book: use the primary mapping above.
3) Anti-Spam / Uniqueness Strategy (Critical)
Companion generation must be non-derivative of the book text and high-variance across catalog.
3.1 Hard Rules (must enforce)
No copying from assembled book output (no quotes, no summaries).
No long prose blocks > 60 words. (Prefer bullets, tables, prompts.)
No repeated fixed templates across books:
Use a “prompt bank” + “phrase bank” + “layout variants” with randomization.
Fingerprint controls
Each companion gets a companion_fingerprint computed from normalized text.
Reject if collision with any prior companion fingerprint in the same run.
3.2 Structure Variation
Each companion has:
layout_variant_id: e.g. cheatsheet_v1, cheatsheet_v2, tracker_v3, prompts_v2
Randomize:
section order (within constraints)
wording style (brand vocabulary)
count of prompts (10–20)
tracker row labels
3.3 Similarity Gate (simple + effective)
Before writing file, compute:
6-gram overlap against previously generated companions in this batch
Jaccard similarity on token sets
Thresholds:
If 6-gram collisions > N or Jaccard > 0.22 → re-roll (seed tweak)
After K retries (e.g. 5) → fallback to different layout variant
4) Inputs and Source of Truth
Companion generator consumes:
Required
canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml (book_id, archetype_id, brand_id, duration_band, voice_id, seeds)
brand_archetype_registry_v1_2.yaml (emotional_vocabulary, gtm_identity, pricing_posture)
config/niche_brand_voice/{brand_id}.yaml (outcome_vocab, title_bank, tone tokens)
topic registry (topic_id → topic labels) if present
Optional
Teacher bank rules if teacher_mode ≠ composite (for voice phrasing constraints)

V4 Companion Content System — DEV SPEC (v1.0)
1. Core Principle (Non-Negotiable)
Companions are not derivative summaries of the audiobook.
They are orthogonal artifacts that activate, track, or externalize the work.
That’s why this system passes spam review.
2. Companion Types (Canonical Set)
Each book gets exactly 1 primary companion, optionally 1 secondary.
Tier A — Low-Risk (Default, Recommended)
These are safe for every brand + topic.
Type ID	Name	What it is	Spam Risk
practice_log	Practice Log	Structured check-ins tied to sessions	🟢 Very Low
reflection_prompts	Reflection Prompts	Open-ended questions, not summaries	🟢 Very Low
integration_checklist	Integration Checklist	“Did I apply this?” lists	🟢 Very Low
weekly_tracker	7-Day Tracker	Habit or state tracking	🟢 Very Low
Tier B — Medium-Value (Use When Brand Fits)
Type ID	Name	Notes
micro_planner	7–14 Day Planner	Action blocks, not advice
body_map	Somatic Mapping Sheet	Sensation + context
decision_canvas	Decision Worksheet	Values-based decisions
Tier C — Premium / Series-Only
Type ID	Name	Notes
guided_journal	30–60 page journal	Paid / bundle
course_workbook	Structured exercises	Series anchor
3. Canonical Rule: 1 Companion per Book
companion_policy:
  required_per_book: 1
  max_per_book: 2
  default_free_ratio: 0.6
60% free, 40% paid (brand-configurable)
Free ≠ low quality
Paid = depth, not repetition

    type = "practice_log"
elif topic in ["anxiety", "stress", "calm"]:
    type = "body_map"
elif series_id:
    type = "guided_journal"

Deterministic seed = hash(book_id + "companion")

Scope and constraints





Applies to all 24 V4 brands via existing config/publishing/brand_archetype_registry_v1_2.yaml and config/niche_brand_voice/ (one YAML per brand_id). No hardcoded brand list in generator logic; all brand data comes from registry + niche_brand_voice.

1. Companion types and selection (deterministic)

Canonical set (merge of both specs):







Type ID



Name



Output file



Use when

1-Page Cheat Sheet



cheatsheet.md



Default / general wellness / mixed topics

7-Day Tracker

journal_prompts.md

Rule: At least 1 companion per book; max 2. Primary type chosen by topic + duration_band (see below). Optional secondary only when spec allows (e.g. Type B + Type A for anxiety).

Topic → primary type mapping (deterministic):





anxiety, stress, panic, nervous system, PTSD-like → tracker_7day (optional + cheat_sheet)



burnout, productivity, ADHD, procrastination → tracker_7day (optional + cheat_sheet)



grief, depression, heartbreak, emotional pain → journal_prompts (+ optional cheat_sheet)



Relationships, boundaries, conflict → journal_prompts (+ optional cheat_sheet)



Identity, creative, purpose → journal_prompts or tracker_7day (e.g. by duration_band)



Else / general wellness → cheat_sheet

New module: phoenix_v4/companions/companion_selector.py





Inputs: book_id, archetype_id, brand_id, default_topic (from registry), duration_band, optional series_id from plan.



Output: companion_plan: companion_id, type (cheat_sheet | tracker_7day | journal_prompts), layout_variant_id (e.g. cheatsheet_v1, tracker_v2), pricing_tier (free | paid), page_target.



Determinism: companion_seed = hash(book_id + "companion" + type + layout_variant_id) (e.g. SHA256 truncated to 32 bits or use hashlib.sha256(...).hexdigest()[:16]). No random; same book → same companion type and variant every time.

Brand-level overrides (optional, non-breaking): If registry gains a per-archetype block companion_defaults (e.g. primary_type, free_ratio, max_pages_free), selector uses it; otherwise use global defaults. Not required for v1.0.



2. Inputs and data flow

flowchart LR
  subgraph inputs [Inputs]
    P[canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml]
    R[brand_archetype_registry_v1_2.yaml]
    V[config/niche_brand_voice per brand_id]
    B[content_banks optional per brand_id]
  end
  subgraph gen [Generator]
    S[companion_selector]
    G[generate_companions.py]
    F[fingerprint and gates]
  end
  subgraph out [Outputs]
    M[companions/book_id/companion_manifest.yaml]
    C[companions/book_id/cheatsheet.md or tracker_7day.md or journal_prompts.md]
    Rpt[companions/_batch/companion_generation_report.json]
  end
  P --> S
  R --> S
  S --> G
  V --> G
  B --> G
  G --> F
  F --> M
  F --> C
  G --> Rpt





Required: canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml, brand_archetype_registry_v1_2.yaml, config/niche_brand_voice/{brand_id}.yaml (all 24 brands already have a file; generator loads by brand_id from plan).



Optional: content_banks/{brand_id}/cheatsheet_bullets.yaml, tracker_labels.yaml, prompt_bank.yaml, micro_phrases.yaml. If present, generator selects/combines deterministically; else use built-in generic banks (short bullets/prompts only, no paragraphs).



3. Output layout and manifest schema

Directory layout:

companions/
  {book_id}/
    companion_manifest.yaml
    cheatsheet.md   # or tracker_7day.md or journal_prompts.md (one per companion)
  _batch/
    companion_generation_report.json

companion_manifest.yaml (per book):





book_id, brand_id, archetype_id, voice_id, duration_band



pricing_mode: free | paid (from duration_band + optional registry; e.g. micro_sessions → free default)



companions: list of { companion_id, type, layout_variant_id, seed, output_path, fingerprint, gates: { jaccard, sixgram_collisions } }

Content file rules (anti-spam):





No paragraph > 60 words; prefer bullets, tables, checkboxes, short prompts.



No text copied from assembled book; no “In this book you learned…” or chapter summaries.



Cheat sheet: sections “What to Notice”, “Do This Today”, “If You Get Stuck”, “One Phrase” (bullet-only).



Tracker: table grid (e.g. daily: body signal, one micro-action, 1 reflection line); no explanatory prose.



Journal pack: 10–20 prompts, grouped; prompts short and high-variance.



4. Anti-spam and uniqueness (hard gates)





Fingerprint: For each generated companion text, compute companion_fingerprint (e.g. SHA256 of normalized text). Reject if collision with any already-generated companion in the same batch run.



No copy from book: Generator never reads assembled book output; it only uses plan metadata, registry, niche_brand_voice, and content banks.



Structure variation: layout_variant_id (e.g. cheatsheet_v1/v2, tracker_v1/v2/v3) plus deterministic seed drives section order and wording style from brand vocabulary (emotional_vocabulary, outcome_vocab, title_bank from niche_brand_voice).



Similarity gate (before writing):





Compute 6-gram set and Jaccard vs. all previously generated companions in batch.



If 6-gram collisions > N (e.g. 15) or Jaccard > 0.22 → re-roll: tweak seed (e.g. seed + retry_count) and regenerate.



After K retries (e.g. 5) → switch to different layout_variant_id and retry.



Reuse patterns from phoenix_v4/tools/content_analysis/exercise_intro_similarity_scan.py (_ngrams, jaccard) for 6-gram and Jaccard; add normalization (e.g. strip, lower, single spaces) for companion text.



5. Generator tool and CLI

New script: phoenix_v4/tools/generate_companions.py

CLI (example):

python3 phoenix_v4/tools/generate_companions.py \
  --plans phoenix_v4/plans/canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml \
  --registry config/publishing/brand_archetype_registry_v1_2.yaml \
  --brand-voice-root config/niche_brand_voice \
  --output companions \
  --seed 0 \
  --min-per-book 1 \
  --max-per-book 1 \
  --pricing-mode auto \
  --dry-run





--plans: path to canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml (or subset).



--registry: brand archetype registry path.



--brand-voice-root: directory containing {brand_id}.yaml; loader uses plan’s brand_id to load the right file for all 24 brands.



--output: root for companions/ (e.g. companions/).



--seed: global seed for any extra randomization (e.g. folded into companion_seed).



--min-per-book / --max-per-book: 1 and 1 for “exactly one companion per book” by default.



--pricing-mode: auto (e.g. micro_sessions → free, deep_dives → paid) or free / paid override.



--dry-run: resolve companion type and layout for each book, print plan, do not write files.

Deterministic seed per companion:
companion_seed = hash(book_id + "companion" + companion_type + layout_variant_id + str(global_seed)) (e.g. via hashlib), then use this seed to select from banks and order sections so the same book always yields the same companion text until layout_variant is changed by retry logic.



6. Content banks (optional)





Location: content_banks/{brand_id}/ with files such as cheatsheet_bullets.yaml, tracker_labels.yaml, prompt_bank.yaml, micro_phrases.yaml.



Contract: Each entry 1–2 lines max; no paragraphs; 100–300 items per bank for high variance. If a bank exists for the plan’s brand_id, generator selects/combines entries deterministically (seed-based indices); otherwise fall back to built-in generic banks so all 24 brands run without requiring banks on day one.



No content team in critical path: v1.0 works with generic fallback; content team can add brand-specific banks later for differentiation.



7. QA script (non-blocking)

New script: phoenix_v4/ci/companion_similarity_report.py





Input: companions/ tree (all companion_manifest.yaml + content files).



Checks: (1) Pairwise 6-gram/Jaccard within batch; flag pairs above threshold. (2) Flag any companion containing a paragraph > 60 words. (3) Flag overly repetitive openings (e.g. same first 50 chars across many companions).



Output: Summary to stdout or a small report file (e.g. companions/_batch/similarity_report.json). Exit 0 always (non-blocking). Later, CI can optionally fail on thresholds if desired.



8. Pricing logic (metadata only)





free: Default for micro_sessions or when pricing_mode=free; lead magnet.



paid: Default for deep_dives / mid_form when pricing_mode=auto or pricing_mode=paid. Price not generated by this tool; stored as pricing_mode in manifest for downstream (e.g. PDF/EPUB store). Rule of thumb: companion price ≤ 40% of audiobook price (documented, not enforced in generator).



9. File and code touchpoints







Item



Action





phoenix_v4/companions/



New package: __init__.py, companion_selector.py (topic→type, layout variant, seed)





phoenix_v4/tools/generate_companions.py

phoenix_v4/tools/content_analysis/exercise_intro_similarity_scan.py



Reuse _ngrams, jaccard (or copy into companions util) for similarity gate and QA





phoenix_v4/ci/companion_similarity_report.py



New: scan companions/, report collisions and long paragraphs; exit 0

Optional later: add companion_defaults per archetype (primary_type, free_ratio). Not required for v1.0.

Read-only: one YAML per brand (24 files); generator loads by plan’s brand_id

Optional: add when content team provides banks; generator checks existence and uses per-brand banks



10. Summary





All brands: Selection and generation are driven entirely by book_id, archetype_id, brand_id, duration_band, and registry + niche_brand_voice; no brand-specific branches.



Deterministic: Same book → same companion type, layout variant, and text (unless retry changes layout variant).



Non-derivative: Generator never reads assembled book content; only plan metadata and brand/topic data.



Safe for scale: Fingerprint + 6-gram/Jaccard gates limit similarity; optional content banks give variance without per-book authoring.



Deliverables: companion_selector.py, generate_companions.py, companion_similarity_report.py, manifest schema, and output layout under companions/{book_id}/ plus companions/_batch/ report.

Here’s the clean plan that won’t blow up your pipeline or spam risk.
How many CTAs per book?
Rule
Exactly 1 primary CTA per book (always)
Optional 1 secondary CTA only for longer durations (and only if it’s “low-friction”)
By duration band
micro_sessions → 1 CTA
mid_form → 1 CTA
deep_dives → 2 CTAs max (primary + secondary)
Why: more CTAs increases repetition risk + lowers conversion quality. One strong CTA per book is safer and converts better.
What is the CTA for?
Two distinct CTA families:
A) “Free companion” CTA (default)
Links to one free text companion (cheat sheet / tracker / prompts)
Lowest spam risk
Highest completion + email capture potential
B) “Exercise app” CTA (conditional)
Only if the book slots a specific exercise
CTA offers the HTML mini-app for that exact exercise
This is the cleanest way to make “37 exercise apps offered anytime the exercise is slotted” true.
CTA placement plan (simple + deterministic)
Always include the primary CTA in one fixed slot
Pick one and never vary by book type (consistency reduces bugs):
Recommended: final integration / end CTA slot (your system already supports per-chapter integration areas)
Secondary CTA (deep_dives only)
Put it in mid-book (e.g., after first major practice chapter), but keep it identical placement rule across all deep_dives.
Mapping logic (what CTA a book gets)
Primary CTA selection (per book)
Deterministic mapping based on:
default_topic (from archetype registry)
duration_band
series_id (if present)
If the book contains any slotted exercise that has an app:
Primary CTA = Get the free exercise app (exercise-specific)
Else:
Primary CTA = Get the free companion pack (text companion)
Secondary CTA (deep_dives only)
If primary = exercise app → secondary = companion pack
If primary = companion pack → secondary = exercise app only if a slotted exercise app exists

Allowed

Short answer: yes — but lightly, and only at the plan policy level, not as per-book content.
You do not want CTA copy or exact placements exploding your planner or hurting determinism.
Here’s the correct, spam-safe architecture.

CTA PLANNING — WHAT GOES IN THE PLANNER (AND WHAT MUST NOT)
You’re planning CTA entitlements and limits, not CTA text.
Think of CTAs the same way you treat:

duration_band
exercise slots
series rules
They are structural allowances, not content.
1️⃣ What the planner MUST plan
The planner must decide how many CTAs are allowed and which classes, so the assembler can act deterministically.
Per-book CTA policy (derived, not authored)
From existing plan inputs:
duration_band
exercise_slots[]
book_id
The planner produces a CTA_POLICY block per book.
Example (implicit, not stored as prose)
cta_policy:
  exercise_ctas:
    enabled: true        # always true if exercises exist
  text_ctas:
    max: 1               # micro / mid
or
cta_policy:
  exercise_ctas:
    enabled: true
  text_ctas:
    max: 2               # deep_dives
    priority:
      - companion_workbook
      - secondary_free_asset
⚠️ No CTA copy
⚠️ No URLs
⚠️ No brand messaging
Just counts + ordering rules.

2️⃣ What the planner MUST NOT do
🚫 Do not:
Assign CTA text
Decide exact CTA wording
Decide which exercise app appears (that’s exercise_id–based)
Hardcode CTA placement strings
Those belong downstream.
3️⃣ How spam safety is guaranteed
Why this works
CTA counts are bounded and deterministic
Exercise CTAs are contextual, not promotional
Text CTAs are structurally sparse
Placement is fixed by rules, not creative choice
This avoids:
CTA clustering
Variable CTA density
CTA collisions across books
“Marketing pattern” detection
4️⃣ Where CTA placement is actually enforced
Layer	Responsibility
Planner	Declares CTA limits + order (policy only)
Assembler	Injects CTAs at fixed locations
Exercise system	Injects app CTA immediately after exercise
Content team	Supplies CTA copy templates
Ops / config	Supplies URLs, landing pages
Planner never sees URLs.
Assembler never decides how many.
This separation is why it scales.
5️⃣ Spread logic (important)
You do not need to “spread” CTAs randomly.
Spam systems care about:

density
positioning
repetition patterns
Your design already avoids flags because:
Exercise CTAs are contextual tools
Text CTAs are:
max 1 (short books)
max 2 (deep dives)
always in predictable, non-intrusive positions
Predictable > random for audit safety.
6️⃣ Final locked rule set (tell dev this verbatim)
CTA planning is declarative, not creative.
The planner defines CTA entitlement (counts + order) based on duration_band and exercise presence.
The assembler enforces placement.
Exercise CTAs are injected per exercise.
Text CTAs are injected only at intro-boundary and end-of-book.
No CTA text, URLs, or copy appear in the planner.

Here's how freebies should work inside your v1.2 catalog — from a marketing perspective, not just a technical one.

**The spec is mechanically correct. The marketing logic needs one adjustment.**

Your companion workbook system is well-designed: separate SKU, authored (not assembled), teacher-led, V3-style, bundle-eligible, CTA placement locked. All good. But the freebie strategy as written treats freebies as a *generosity gesture*. It should be treated as a **conversion engine**.

**The freebie funnel you should be running:**

Every freebie exists to do exactly one job: move a listener from a free asset to a paid purchase. That's it. The way this maps to your catalog:

**Tier 1 — Free companion workbooks (deep dives only)**
This is already in your spec and it's correct. A $0 workbook CTA placed after the intro of a $19.99–$27.99 deep dive creates a reciprocity loop. The listener gets a free practice tool, feels invested in the teacher, and is primed for the next series volume. Keep this exactly as designed — mandatory for deep dives, always free, never sold.

**Tier 2 — Free micro-sessions as brand entry points (this is what's missing)**
For each of the 24 brands, you should designate 2–3 of the 42 books as **permanently free**. These are your shortest micro-sessions (15–20 min), priced at $0.00 on Google Play and distributed free through INaudio. They serve as the top of your funnel — a listener discovers panic_first_aid through a free 18-minute grounding session, completes it (high completion rate because it's short), gets recommended the paid series, and converts.

This means your actual catalog math becomes: 1,008 total books, ~48–72 free (2–3 per brand), ~936–960 paid. The free titles aren't lost revenue — they're customer acquisition at $0 CAC.

**Tier 3 — Free exercise HTML apps (already in your spec)**
The 39 exercise apps with CTAs injected after exercise slots. These are engagement tools, not revenue tools. They keep listeners inside your ecosystem between book purchases. Correct as designed.

**How to plan freebies inside the 1,008 BookPlan generator:**

Add a pricing_tier field to each BookPlan:

yaml
pricing_tier: free | standard | premium

# Free selection rules:
# - Max 3 free books per brand
# - Must be micro_sessions duration_band
# - Must be standalone (never a series volume)
# - Must have high somatic_slot_probability
# - Must use lead_voice (brand recognition)
# - Never free a Book 1 of a series (that's your on-ramp to paid)


**The counterintuitive rule: never make Series Book 1 free.** Most publishers give away Book 1 to hook readers into a series. For your catalog, that's wrong. Your micro-session standalones are better freebies because they're complete experiences that demonstrate the teacher and brand in 15 minutes, they have the highest completion rates (which feeds the algorithm), they don't devalue the series architecture, and a listener who finishes a free standalone and then discovers a 7-book series will pay full price for Book 1 because they already trust the voice.

**Freebie allocation across clusters:**

| Cluster | Brands | Free Titles | Rationale |
|---------|--------|-------------|-----------|
| Nervous System | 9 | 27 (3 each) | Highest-intent keywords; free titles become top-of-funnel |
| Productivity/ADHD | 6 | 12 (2 each) | ADHD audience needs low-barrier entry |
| Vitality | 3 | 6 (2 each) | Standard allocation |
| Relationships | 3 | 6 (2 each) | Standard allocation |
| Identity/Creative | 2 | 4 (2 each) | Standard allocation |
| Gen Z | 1 | 3 | Price-sensitive audience; more freebies = more trial |
| Wisdom | 1 | 2 | Standard allocation |
| **Total** | **24** | **60** | **~6% of catalog is free** |

**Google Play pricing rules for freebies:**

Remember the compliance constraint — your Google Play price must be ≤ everywhere else. If a title is free on Google Play, it must be free on INaudio partners too. This is fine for designated freebies but means you can't do "free on Google Play, paid on Spotify" as a platform arbitrage strategy.

**The CTA planning integration is already correct.** Your spec says the planner declares CTA entitlements (counts + order), the assembler enforces placement, and no CTA copy lives in the planner. That's the right separation. The only addition: for free titles, the CTA at end-of-book should point to the *paid series* in the same brand, not to a companion workbook (free titles don't get companion workbooks — they *are* the freebie).

**What changes in the implementation plan:** Nothing structural. Add pricing_tier to the BookPlan schema, add free-title selection rules to the generator's allocation logic, and document the "never free a Series Book 1" rule in the ops doc. The registry, validators, assembler, and engine are all untouched.

This turns your freebie strategy from "nice to have" into a measurable acquisition channel with a clear path: free standalone → paid series → companion workbook → repeat purchase across brands.

You said:

lookk good?: CTA System — Implementation Plan

Rules (locked)





Exercise CTA: One per slotted exercise; placed immediately after the exercise content block. Unlimited; does not count toward text CTA limits.



Text CTAs:  





micro_sessions / mid_form: 1 text CTA only, at end of book.  



deep_dives: 2 text CTAs: #1 = companion workbook (free), after intro / before Chapter 1; #2 = optional secondary, at end of book.



Companion workbook: Always free; first text CTA for deep_dives. No selling in plan.



Planning: Declarative only (CTA policy: counts + order). No CTA copy, URLs, or wording in the planner.



1. CTA policy (declarative)

Policy is derived at assembly time from:





duration_band (from cta_manifest or plan.metadata.duration_band or derived from book_size/duration),



presence of exercise slots (exercise CTAs enabled when any chapter has an exercise),



optional cta_manifest per book for overrides.

No new planner schema. No CTA text in plans.

Derivation:





If duration_band == "deep_dives": text CTAs max = 2, order = [companion_workbook, secondary_free_asset].



Else (micro_sessions, mid_form, or unknown): text CTAs max = 1, placement = end_of_book only.



Exercise CTAs: enabled whenever the assembler renders an exercise (exercise_id present).



2. Exercise app registry

New file: config/exercises/exercise_app_registry.json

Schema (per exercise_id):

{
  "ahjan_anxiety_e02": {
    "app_slug": "box_breathing_4444",
    "app_url": "/apps/box_breathing_4444/index.html",
    "safety_level": "basic",
    "duration_class": "short"
  }
}





app_url: Path or URL for the HTML app (relative or absolute; assembler emits as link target).



safety_level / duration_class: Optional for future filtering.

Populate from the 37 somatic exercises (and any canonical exercise IDs used in V4). One registry entry per exercise that has an HTML app. If an exercise_id is not in the registry, do not inject an exercise CTA for it.

Loader: Small helper in assembler or shared util: load_exercise_app_registry(path) -> dict. Default path: config/exercises/exercise_app_registry.json.



3. CTA manifest (per book, optional)

Path: cta_manifests/{book_id}.yaml

Schema:

book_id: anxiety_genz_042
duration_band: deep_dives

text_ctas:
  - order: 1
    type: companion_workbook
    pricing: free
    placement: mid_book   # after intro, before Ch1 (deep_dives only)
  - order: 2
    type: secondary_free_asset
    placement: end_book

When to generate: New tool or step (e.g. phoenix_v4/tools/generate_cta_manifests.py) that reads canonical_1008_bookplans (and optionally existing V4 plans), derives duration_band per book, and writes cta_manifests/{book_id}.yaml with the rules above. For deep_dives, always include companion_workbook as order 1.

When assembling: If cta_manifests/{book_id}.yaml exists, load it and use it for text CTA count, order, and placement. If not, derive policy from plan.metadata.duration_band or plan book_size/duration (e.g. long + standard -> treat as deep_dives for CTA purposes).



4. Assembler injection points

flowchart LR
  subgraph book [Book structure]
    FM[front_matter]
    CTA1[CTA after intro]
    CH1[Ch1]
    CH2[Ch2]
    CTA_E1[Exercise CTA]
    CHN[Ch N]
    CTA_END[CTA end]
    BM[back_matter]
  end
  FM --> CTA1
  CTA1 --> CH1
  CH1 --> CH2
  CH2 --> CTA_E1
  CTA_E1 --> CHN
  CHN --> CTA_END
  CTA_END --> BM

A) Exercise CTA (slot-level)

Where: phoenix_v4/assembler/slot_assembler.py, immediately after the block that sets slot_content = exercise_text for slot_07_practice (and after motif injection if present), before appending to chapter parts.

Logic:





When rendering a slot that is slot_07_practice and has an exercise_id (from exercise_plan).



After setting slot_content to the exercise text, look up exercise_id in the exercise app registry.



If found, append a fixed, short CTA block (e.g. one line: “Use the free guided app for this exercise → [Open Exercise Tool]”) to the content that is appended for this slot. Use a single template; no brand copy here.



Do not add any CTA when the exercise is not in the registry.

Contract: CTA block length ≤ 20 words; no variation by book; link target from registry (app_url).

Data flow: assemble_chapter_slots already has exercise_plan and exercise_id. Pass the registry (or its path) into the assembler so slot_assembler can resolve app_url. Option: pass a callable get_exercise_cta(exercise_id) -> optional str so slot_assembler stays agnostic of registry path.

B) Text CTA after intro (deep_dives only)

Where: phoenix_v4/assembler/assemble_v4.py. After building front_matter, before building the first chapter.

Options:





Option 1 (recommended): Extend Book with an optional cta_after_intro: Optional[str]. When creating the Book object, if CTA policy says “text CTA #1 after intro” (deep_dives + companion_workbook), set cta_after_intro to a single CTA block (template: companion workbook, ≤ 35 words). In Book.to_markdown(), after appending front_matter, append cta_after_intro if set, then append chapters.



Option 2: Inject into front_matter string: front_matter = front_matter + "\n\n" + cta_block. Simpler but mixes CTA with intro content.

Policy: Only set cta_after_intro when duration_band == "deep_dives" and text CTAs include companion_workbook as first. Use cta_manifest or derived policy.

C) Text CTA end of book

Where: Same Book and to_markdown(). Add optional cta_end_of_book: Optional[str].

Logic:





micro_sessions / mid_form: One text CTA at end only → set cta_end_of_book to the companion workbook CTA block (same template as “free companion”).



deep_dives: Second text CTA at end → set cta_end_of_book to the secondary CTA block (or companion if only one text CTA is configured; policy says two, so first is after intro, second is end).

In Book.to_markdown(), after appending the last chapter and before appending back_matter, append cta_end_of_book if set.

Order in to_markdown():





Title, subtitle



front_matter



cta_after_intro (if set)



Chapters



cta_end_of_book (if set)



back_matter



5. CTA copy (templates)

Rule: No “In this book…”, “Chapter…”, “You learned…”. Short, high-variance later; v1 one template per type.





Exercise CTA (single template): e.g. “Use the free guided app for this exercise. [Open Exercise Tool]” (link from registry app_url). ≤ 20 words.



Companion workbook CTA: e.g. “Download the free companion workbook to support this practice. [Get Workbook]”. ≤ 35 words. Link target: e.g. /companions/{book_id} or from config.



Secondary CTA: e.g. “Get more free resources. [See Resources]”. Placeholder until secondary asset type is defined.

Store templates in one small module or YAML (e.g. phoenix_v4/assembler/cta_templates.yaml or constants in phoenix_v4/assembler/cta.py) so copy can be swapped later without touching assembler logic.



6. Where duration_band comes from





Canonical runs: CTA manifest generator writes cta_manifests/{book_id}.yaml from canonical_1008_bookplans (which has duration_band). Assembler loads by plan.book_id.



Non-canonical / ad-hoc plans: Plan may have plan.metadata.duration_band. If not, derive from plan.book_size + plan.duration (e.g. long + standard -> deep_dives) so CTA policy still applies. Fallback: treat as mid_form (1 CTA at end only).



7. File touchpoints







Item



Action





config/exercises/exercise_app_registry.json



New: map exercise_id -> app_slug, app_url, optional safety_level/duration_class. Populate for 37 exercises (and any V4 exercise IDs that have apps).





phoenix_v4/assembler/slot_assembler.py



After rendering slot_07_practice exercise content, if exercise_id in registry, append exercise CTA block (via injected helper or registry lookup).





phoenix_v4/assembler/assemble_v4.py



Before creating Book: resolve CTA policy (from cta_manifest or plan.metadata); set cta_after_intro and cta_end_of_book on Book. Extend Book.to_markdown() to insert them after front_matter and before back_matter.





phoenix_v4/assembler/cta.py (new)



Load exercise app registry; load cta_manifest by book_id; derive policy when manifest missing; render CTA blocks from templates (exercise, companion, secondary).





cta_manifests/



New dir. Filled by generate_cta_manifests.py (or equivalent) from canonical plans.





phoenix_v4/tools/generate_cta_manifests.py (new)



Read canonical_1008_bookplans (or plan list); for each book_id write cta_manifests/{book_id}.yaml with duration_band and text_ctas (deep_dives: companion_workbook + secondary; else 1 at end). No CTA copy in manifest.



8. Guardrails





Never inject text CTA mid-chapter.



Never inject text CTA immediately after an exercise (exercise CTA is the only CTA there).



Never exceed 1 text CTA for micro/mid, 2 for deep_dives.



Never sell companion workbooks in CTA copy; always “free”.



Never reference “this book” or “chapter” in CTA text.



9. Summary





Planner: No schema change. CTA policy is derived (duration_band + exercise presence) or read from optional cta_manifests/{book_id}.yaml.



Assembler: Exercise CTA after each exercise slot (when exercise in registry); text CTA #1 after intro for deep_dives (companion workbook); text CTA at end (companion for micro/mid, secondary for deep_dives). Book gains cta_after_intro and cta_end_of_book; to_markdown() inserts them at fixed positions.



New artifacts: exercise_app_registry.json, cta_manifests per book, CTA template module or YAML, generate_cta_manifests script.

2️⃣ generate_cta_manifests.py — Pseudocode
load canonical_1008_bookplans.yaml

for book in plans:
    book_id = book.book_id
    duration_band = book.duration_band
    is_series = book.series_id is not None

    manifest = {
        "book_id": book_id,
        "duration_band": duration_band,
        "text_ctas": []
    }

    if duration_band == "deep_dives":
        manifest["text_ctas"].append({
            "order": 1,
            "type": "companion_workbook",
            "pricing": "free",
            "placement": "after_intro"
        })

        manifest["text_ctas"].append({
            "order": 2,
            "type": "secondary_free_asset",
            "placement": "end_book"
        })

    else:
        # micro_sessions / mid_form
        if companion_exists(book_id):
            manifest["text_ctas"].append({
                "order": 1,
                "type": "companion_workbook",
                "pricing": "free",
                "placement": "end_book"
            })
        else:
            manifest["text_ctas"].append({
                "order": 1,
                "type": "secondary_free_asset",
                "placement": "end_book"
            })

    write cta_manifests/{book_id}.yaml
Rules enforced here
Max 2 CTAs
No mid-chapter CTAs
Deep dives always get workbook first
No selling logic

Allowed Secondary Free Assets
